</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Children</th><td class="infobox-data">3</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header">Signature</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><span class="infobox-signature skin-invert" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Sergey_Brin_google_signature.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Sergey_Brin_google_signature.svg/250px-Sergey_Brin_google_signature.svg.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="48" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Sergey_Brin_google_signature.svg/330px-Sergey_Brin_google_signature.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="165" data-file-height="53" /></a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Sergey Mikhailovich Brin</b><sup id="cite&#95;ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>a<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> (Russian: <span lang="ru">Сергей Михайлович Брин</span>; born August 21, 1973) is an American <a href="/wiki/Computer_scientist" title="Computer scientist">computer scientist</a> and businessman who co-founded <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> with <a href="/wiki/Larry_Page" title="Larry Page">Larry Page</a>. He was the president of Google's parent company, <a href="/wiki/Alphabet_Inc." title="Alphabet Inc.">Alphabet Inc.</a>, until stepping down from the role on December 3, 2019.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He and Page remain at Alphabet as co-founders, <a href="/wiki/Controlling_shareholder" class="mw-redirect" title="Controlling shareholder">controlling shareholders</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Board_members" class="mw-redirect" title="Board members">board members</a>. Brin is a <a href="/wiki/Centibillionaire" class="mw-redirect" title="Centibillionaire">centibillionaire</a> and among the <a href="/wiki/The_World%27s_Billionaires" title="The World&#39;s Billionaires">richest people in the world</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Bloomberg&#95;3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Forbes&#95;4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Brin immigrated to the United States from the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> at the age of six. He earned his bachelor's degree at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_College_Park" title="University of Maryland, College Park">University of Maryland, College Park</a>, following in his father's and grandfather's<sup id="cite&#95;ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> footsteps by studying mathematics as well as computer science. After graduation, in September 1993, he enrolled in <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> to pursue a PhD in computer science. There he met Page, with whom he built a <a href="/wiki/Web_search_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Web search engine">web search engine</a>. The program became popular at Stanford, and he discontinued his PhD studies to start Google in <a href="/wiki/Susan_Wojcicki" title="Susan Wojcicki">Susan Wojcicki</a>'s garage in <a href="/wiki/Menlo_Park,_California" title="Menlo Park, California">Menlo Park</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2023, he came out of retirement to contribute to AI research at <a href="/wiki/Alphabet_Inc." title="Alphabet Inc.">Alphabet Inc.</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Early_life_and_education">Early life and education</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sergey_Brin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life and education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Sergey Mikhailovich Brin was born into a <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Russia" title="History of the Jews in Russia">Jewish</a> family on August 21, 1973, in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, the capital of <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>. At the time, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russia</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">constituent republic</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Both of Brin's parents, Mikhail and Eugenia Brin (1948–2024), had graduated from <a href="/wiki/Moscow_State_University" title="Moscow State University">Moscow State University</a> (MSU).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> His father is a retired mathematics professor at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_College_Park" title="University of Maryland, College Park">University of Maryland</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and his mother was a researcher at <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Goddard_Space_Flight_Center" title="Goddard Space Flight Center">Goddard Space Flight Center</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Moment&#95;12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moment-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Brin family lived in a three-room apartment in central Moscow, which they also shared with Sergey's paternal grandmother.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Moment&#95;12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moment-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1977, after returning from a mathematics conference in Warsaw, Poland, Mikhail announced that, because of <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Antisemitism in the Soviet Union">antisemitism in the Soviet Union</a>, it was time for the family to emigrate.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Moment&#95;12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moment-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They formally applied for their <a href="/wiki/Exit_visa" class="mw-redirect" title="Exit visa">exit visa</a> in September 1978, and as a result, his father was "promptly fired". For related reasons, his mother had to leave her job. For the next eight months, without any steady income, they were forced to take on temporary jobs as they waited, afraid their request would be denied as it was for many <a href="/wiki/Refuseniks" class="mw-redirect" title="Refuseniks">refuseniks</a>. In May 1979, they were granted their official exit visas and were allowed to leave the country.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Moment&#95;12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moment-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Brin family lived in Vienna and Paris while Mikhail Brin secured a teaching position at the University of Maryland with help from <a href="/wiki/Anatole_Katok" title="Anatole Katok">Anatole Katok</a>. During this time, the Brin family received support and assistance from the <a href="/wiki/HIAS" title="HIAS">Hebrew Immigrant Aid Society</a>. They arrived in the United States on October 25, 1979.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Moment&#95;12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moment-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-hias&#95;16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hias-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>He attended <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt_High_School_(Maryland)" title="Eleanor Roosevelt High School (Maryland)">Eleanor Roosevelt High School</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Moment&#95;12-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moment-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In September 1990, Brin enrolled in the University of Maryland, where he received his <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science" title="Bachelor of Science">Bachelor of Science</a> from the Department of Computer Science in 1993 with honors in <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a> and high honors in mathematics at the age of 19.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-resume&#95;17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-resume-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1993, he <a href="/wiki/Intern" class="mw-redirect" title="Intern">interned</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wolfram_Research" title="Wolfram Research">Wolfram Research</a>, the developers of <a href="/wiki/Wolfram_Mathematica" title="Wolfram Mathematica">Mathematica</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-resume&#95;17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-resume-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Brin began his graduate study in computer science at <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> on a <a href="/wiki/NSF_Graduate_Research_Fellowship_Program" title="NSF Graduate Research Fellowship Program">graduate fellowship from the National Science Foundation</a>, receiving a <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Science" title="Master of Science">Master of Science</a> degree in computer science in 1995.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sergey_Brin&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, he was on leave from his <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">Doctor of Philosophy</a> studies at Stanford.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Search_engine_development">Search engine development</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sergey_Brin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Search engine development"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Schmidt-Brin-Page-20080520.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Schmidt-Brin-Page-20080520.jpg/250px-Schmidt-Brin-Page-20080520.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="190" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Schmidt-Brin-Page-20080520.jpg/500px-Schmidt-Brin-Page-20080520.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2916" data-file-height="2217" /></a><figcaption>Left to right, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Schmidt" title="Eric Schmidt">Eric Schmidt</a>, Brin and <a href="/wiki/Larry_Page" title="Larry Page">Larry Page</a>, 2008</figcaption></figure>
<p>During an orientation for new students at Stanford, he met <a href="/wiki/Larry_Page" title="Larry Page">Larry Page</a>. The two men seemed to disagree on most subjects, but after spending time together they "became intellectual soul-mates and close friends." Brin's focus was on developing data mining systems while Page's was on extending "the concept of inferring the importance of a research paper from its <a href="/wiki/Citation" title="Citation">citations</a> in other papers".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Economist&#95;20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Together, they authored a paper titled "The Anatomy of a Large-Scale <a href="/wiki/Hypertext" title="Hypertext">Hypertextual</a> Web Search Engine".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>To convert the backlink data gathered by Backrub's <a href="/wiki/Web_crawler" title="Web crawler">web crawler</a> into a measure of importance for a given web page, Brin and Page developed the <a href="/wiki/PageRank" title="PageRank">PageRank algorithm</a>, and realized that it could be used to build a <a href="/wiki/Search_engine" title="Search engine">search engine</a> far superior to those existing at the time.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-wiredbirth&#95;22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wiredbirth-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The new algorithm relied on a new kind of technology that analyzed the relevance of the <a href="/wiki/Backlink" title="Backlink">backlinks</a> that connected one Web page to another, and allowed the number of links and their rank, to determine the rank of the page.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Moschovitis&#95;23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moschovitis-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Combining their ideas, they began utilizing Page's dormitory room as a machine laboratory, and extracted spare parts from inexpensive computers to create a device that they used to connect the nascent search engine with Stanford's broadband campus network.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-wiredbirth&#95;22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wiredbirth-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>After filling Page's room with equipment, they then converted Brin's dorm room into an office and programming center, where they tested their new search engine designs on the web. The rapid growth of their project caused Stanford's computing infrastructure to experience problems.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-economist.com&#95;24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist.com-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Page and Brin used Page's basic <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a> programming skills to set up a simple search page for users, as they did not have a web page developer to create anything visually elaborate. They also began using any computer part they could find to assemble the necessary computing power to handle searches by multiple users. As their search engine grew in popularity among Stanford users, it required additional <a href="/wiki/Server_(computing)" title="Server (computing)">servers</a> to process the queries. In August 1996, the initial version of Google was made available on the Stanford Web site.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-wiredbirth&#95;22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wiredbirth-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>By early 1997, the Backrub page described the state as follows:
</p>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:PageRanks-Example.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/PageRanks-Example.svg/250px-PageRanks-Example.svg.png" decoding="async" width="179" height="144" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/PageRanks-Example.svg/330px-PageRanks-Example.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/PageRanks-Example.svg/500px-PageRanks-Example.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="758" data-file-height="611" /></a><figcaption>The mathematical website interlinking that the <a href="/wiki/PageRank" title="PageRank">PageRank</a> algorithm facilitates, illustrated by size-percentage correlation of the circles. The <a href="/wiki/Algorithm" title="Algorithm">algorithm</a> was named after Page himself.</figcaption></figure>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>Some Rough Statistics (from August 29, 1996)</dd>
<dd>Total indexable HTML urls: 75.2306&#160;Million</dd>
<dd>Total content downloaded: 207.022&#160;gigabytes</dd>
<dd>...</dd></dl></dd></dl>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>BackRub is written in Java and Python and runs on several Sun Ultras and Intel Pentiums running <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a>. The primary database is kept on a <a href="/wiki/Sun_Ultra_series" class="mw-redirect" title="Sun Ultra series">Sun Ultra series</a> II with 28GB of disk. Scott Hassan and Alan Steremberg have provided a great deal of very talented implementation help. Sergey Brin has also been very involved and deserves many thanks.
<dl><dd>- Larry Page <span class="nowrap">page<span class="mw-no-invert"><span class="skin-invert" typeof="mw:File"><span title="@"><img alt="@" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/At_sign.svg/20px-At_sign.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/At_sign.svg/40px-At_sign.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="145" data-file-height="145" /></span></span></span>cs.stanford.edu</span><sup id="cite&#95;ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl>
<p>BackRub already exhibited the rudimentary functions and characteristics of a search engine: a query input was entered and it provided a list of backlinks ranked by importance. Page recalled: "We realized that we had a querying tool. It gave you a good overall ranking of pages and ordering of follow-up pages."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-archive.wired.com&#95;26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive.wired.com-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Page said that in mid-1998 they finally realized the further potential of their project: "Pretty soon, we had 10,000 searches a day. And we figured, maybe this is really real."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-economist.com&#95;24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist.com-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Some compared Page and Brin's vision to the impact of <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Gutenberg" title="Johannes Gutenberg">Johannes Gutenberg</a>, the inventor of modern printing:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1244412712">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 32px}.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;margin-top:0}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{padding-left:1.6em}}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>In 1440, Johannes Gutenberg introduced Europe to the mechanical printing press, printing Bibles for mass consumption. The technology allowed for books and manuscripts‍&#8212;‌originally replicated by hand‍&#8212;‌to be printed at a much faster rate, thus spreading knowledge and helping to usher in the European Renaissance<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... Google has done a similar job.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>The comparison was also noted by the authors of <i>The Google Story</i>: "Not since Gutenberg<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... has any new invention empowered individuals, and transformed access to information, as profoundly as Google."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Vise&#95;28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vise-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Also, not long after the two "cooked up their new engine for web searches, they began thinking about information that was at the time beyond the web," such as digitizing books and expanding health information.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-economist.com&#95;24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist.com-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Other_interests">Other interests</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sergey_Brin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Other interests"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Sergey_Brin_(cropped).JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Sergey_Brin_%28cropped%29.JPG/250px-Sergey_Brin_%28cropped%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="180" height="281" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e9/Sergey_Brin_%28cropped%29.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="469" /></a><figcaption>Brin at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">University of California, Berkeley</a> in October 2005</figcaption></figure>
<p>In June 2008, Brin invested $4.5&#160;million in <a href="/wiki/Space_Adventures" title="Space Adventures">Space Adventures</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Space_tourism" title="Space tourism">space tourism</a> company.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Brin and Page jointly own a customized <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767–200</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Dassault/Dornier_Alpha_Jet" title="Dassault/Dornier Alpha Jet">Dassault/Dornier Alpha Jet</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-dornierjet&#95;30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dornierjet-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and pay $1.3&#160;million a year to house them and two <a href="/wiki/Gulfstream_V" title="Gulfstream V">Gulfstream V</a> jets owned by Google executives at <a href="/wiki/Moffett_Federal_Airfield" title="Moffett Federal Airfield">Moffett Federal Airfield</a>. The aircraft has scientific equipment installed by <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> to allow experimental data to be collected in flight.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Brin is a backer of LTA Research &amp; Exploration LLC, an <a href="/wiki/Airship" title="Airship">airship</a> maker company.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In October 2023, LTA's 124-meter long flagship, Pathfinder 1, became the largest airship since the <i><a href="/wiki/LZ_129_Hindenburg" title="LZ 129 Hindenburg">Hindenburg</a></i> to receive clearance for flight testing, permitted over the boundaries of <a href="/wiki/Moffett_Federal_Airfield" title="Moffett Federal Airfield">Moffett Field</a> and neighboring <a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto_Airport" title="Palo Alto Airport">Palo Alto Airport</a>'s airspaces, at a height of up to 460 meters.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Personal_life">Personal life</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sergey_Brin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Personal life"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Sergey_Brin,_Web_2.0_Conference.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Sergey_Brin%2C_Web_2.0_Conference.jpg/250px-Sergey_Brin%2C_Web_2.0_Conference.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Sergey_Brin%2C_Web_2.0_Conference.jpg/500px-Sergey_Brin%2C_Web_2.0_Conference.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="667" /></a><figcaption>Brin in 2005 at the <a href="/wiki/Web_2.0" title="Web 2.0">Web 2.0</a> Conference</figcaption></figure>
<p>Brin was raised Jewish, but is not religious.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Questionable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (December 2024)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In May 2007, Brin married <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotech analyst</a> and entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Anne_Wojcicki" title="Anne Wojcicki">Anne Wojcicki</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">the Bahamas</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-WP&#95;36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They had a son in late 2008 and a daughter in late 2011.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In August 2013, it was announced that Brin and his wife were living separately after Brin had an extramarital affair with a <a href="/wiki/Google_Glass" title="Google Glass">Google Glass</a> colleague.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In June 2015, Brin and Wojcicki finalized their divorce.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Grigoriadis&#95;42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grigoriadis-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On November 7, 2018, he married <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Shanahan" title="Nicole Shanahan">Nicole Shanahan</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Legal_technology" title="Legal technology">legal tech</a> founder.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BI220617&#95;43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BI220617-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They have a daughter, born in late 2018.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Brin and Shanahan separated on December 15, 2021, and Brin filed for divorce on January 4, 2022.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BI220617&#95;43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BI220617-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In summer 2023, the divorce was finalized.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Journal" class="mw-redirect" title="Wall Street Journal">Wall Street Journal</a></i> reported that a reason for the breakup was a "brief affair" in 2021 between Shanahan and <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">Elon Musk</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Brin's mother, Eugenia, has been diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Parkinson%27s_disease" title="Parkinson&#39;s disease">Parkinson's disease</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2008, he decided to make a donation to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland_School_of_Medicine" title="University of Maryland School of Medicine">University of Maryland School of Medicine</a>, where his mother has received treatment.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to <i>Forbes</i>, Brin has donated over $1&#160;billion to fund research on the disease.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Brin and Wojcicki, although separated, jointly ran The Brin Wojcicki Foundation until 2014. Since then, Brin has used the <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Brin_Family_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Sergey Brin Family Foundation">Sergey Brin Family Foundation</a> and a donor-advised fund for his philanthropic giving.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-dynamodata&#95;50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dynamodata-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They donated extensively to <a href="/wiki/The_Michael_J._Fox_Foundation" title="The Michael J. Fox Foundation">The Michael J. Fox Foundation</a> and in 2009 gave $1&#160;million to support the <a href="/wiki/HIAS" title="HIAS">Hebrew Immigrant Aid Society</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-hias&#95;16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hias-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Brin is a donor to <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> candidates and organizations, having donated $5,000 to <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama_2012_presidential_campaign" title="Barack Obama 2012 presidential campaign">2012 reelection campaign</a> and $30,800 to the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_National_Committee" title="Democratic National Committee">DNC</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Brin attended the <a href="/wiki/Second_inauguration_of_Donald_Trump" title="Second inauguration of Donald Trump">second inauguration of Donald Trump</a>, sitting alongside Donald Trump supporters and other tech moguls.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In December 2025, Brin and Page, worth a combined $520 billion, terminated or moved out of California 60 limited liability companies that hold their assets.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NYT&#95;2026-01-09&#95;54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_2026-01-09-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Brin is the owner of the <a href="/wiki/Superyacht" title="Superyacht">superyacht</a> <a href="/wiki/Dragonfly_(yacht)" title="Dragonfly (yacht)"><i>Dragonfly</i></a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Awards_and_accolades">Awards and accolades</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sergey_Brin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Awards and accolades"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2002–2009"><span id="2002.E2.80.932009"></span>2002–2009</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sergey_Brin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2002–2009"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>In 2002, Brin, along with Larry Page, was named in the <i><a href="/wiki/MIT_Technology_Review" title="MIT Technology Review">MIT Technology Review</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Innovators_Under_35" title="Innovators Under 35">TR100</a>, as one of the top 100 innovators in the world under the age of 35.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2003, both Brin and Page received an <a href="/wiki/Honorary_degree" title="Honorary degree">honorary</a> MBA from <a href="/wiki/IE_Business_School" title="IE Business School">IE Business School</a> "for embodying the entrepreneurial spirit and lending momentum to the creation of new businesses...".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2003, Brin and Page were both Award Recipients and National Finalists for the EY Entrepreneur of the Year Award.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2004, they received the <a href="/wiki/Marconi_Prize" title="Marconi Prize">Marconi Prize</a>, and were elected Fellows of the <a href="/wiki/Marconi_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Marconi Foundation">Marconi Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The two men were "cited for the invention that has fundamentally changed the way information is retrieved today."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2004, Brin received the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Achievement" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy of Achievement">American Academy of Achievement</a>'s Golden Plate Award with Larry Page at a ceremony in Chicago, Illinois.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Goldenplate&#95;61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goldenplate-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2006, Brin was one of the inaugural class of winners of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Immigrants_Award" title="Great Immigrants Award">Great Immigrants Award</a> named by <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Corporation_of_New_York" title="Carnegie Corporation of New York">Carnegie Corporation of New York</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Since_2009">Since 2009</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sergey_Brin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Since 2009"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>In November 2009, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> named Brin and Page the fifth most powerful people in the world.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Earlier that same year, in February, Brin was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">National Academy of Engineering</a>, which is "among the highest professional distinctions accorded to an engineer ... [and] honors those who have made outstanding contributions to engineering research, practice...".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He was selected specifically, "for leadership in development of rapid indexing and retrieval of relevant information from the World Wide Web".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In their "Profiles" of Fellows, the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> included a number of earlier awards:<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1244412712" /><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>he was a featured speaker at the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a> and the Technology, Entertainment and Design Conference. ... <i><a href="/wiki/PC_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="PC Magazine">PC Magazine</a></i> has praised Google in the Top 100 Web Sites and Search Engines (1998) and awarded Google the Technical Excellence Award, for Innovation in Web Application Development in 1999. In 2000, Google earned a <a href="/wiki/Webby_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Webby Award">Webby Award</a>, a People's Voice Award for technical achievement, and in 2001, was awarded Outstanding Search Service, Best Image Search Engine, Best Design, Most Webmaster Friendly Search Engine, and Best Search Feature at the Search Engine Watch Awards.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote></li>
<li>As of September 2024, Brin is the tenth-richest person in the world according to Bloomberg, with an estimated net worth of $135&#160;billion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Appearances_in_film">Appearances in film</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sergey_Brin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Appearances in film"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

</p>

<li id="cite&#95;note-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-35">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333433106" /><cite id="CITEREFBloom2013" class="citation web cs1">Bloom, Nate (September 10, 2013). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jewishtampa.com/jews-in-the-news/jews-in-the-news-diane-von-furstenburg-michael-kors-and-barbara-hershey">"Jews in the News: Diane Von Furstenburg, Michael Kors and Barbara Hershey"</a>. <i>Tampa Jewish Federation</i>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20191105023447/https://www.jewishtampa.com/jews-in-the-news/jews-in-the-news-diane-von-furstenburg-michael-kors-and-barbara-hershey">Archived</a> from the original on November 5, 2019<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">November 5,</span> 2019</span>. <q>Brin's Jewish parents left the former Soviet Union in 1979, tired of the anti-Semitism which had impeded their respective academic careers and despairing of the prospects for their son. Brin wed biologist Wojcicki in 2007 and the couple now have two children. Neither Brin nor Wojcicki (whose mother is Jewish) are religious, but they did have some Jewish touches at their secular wedding: a chuppah-- and Brin stepped on a glass</q></cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Tampa+Jewish+Federation&amp;rft.atitle=Jews+in+the+News%3A+Diane+Von+Furstenburg%2C+Michael+Kors+and+Barbara+Hershey&amp;rft.date=2013-09-10&amp;rft.aulast=Bloom&amp;rft.aufirst=Nate&amp;rft&#95;id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.jewishtampa.com%2Fjews-in-the-news%2Fjews-in-the-news-diane-von-furstenburg-michael-kors-and-barbara-hershey&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASergey+Brin" class="Z3988"></span></span>

<li id="cite&#95;note-NYT&#95;2026-01-09-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-NYT_2026-01-09_54-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333433106" /><cite id="CITEREFMacSchleiferKnight2026" class="citation news cs1">Mac, Ryan; Schleifer, Theodore; Knight, Heather (January 9, 2026). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2026/01/09/technology/google-founders-california-wealth-tax.html">"Google Guys Say Bye to California"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Times">New York Times</a></i>. <q>In the 10 days before Christmas, an entity connected to Mr. Brin, 52, terminated or moved 15 California limited liability companies that oversee some of his business interests and investments out of the state, according to documents seen by The New York Times. Seven of the companies — including those that appear to manage one of Mr. Brin's superyachts and his interest in a private air terminal at San Jose's international airport — were converted into Nevada entities. ... Another entity jointly managed by Mr. Brin and Mr. Page moved out of California and to Nevada on Christmas Eve, according to a filing seen by The Times. The Google founders' shrinking connections to California underscore the impact of a potential ballot measure that would affect the state's wealthiest residents.</q></cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=New+York+Times&amp;rft.atitle=Google+Guys+Say+Bye+to+California&amp;rft.date=2026-01-09&amp;rft.aulast=Mac&amp;rft.aufirst=Ryan&amp;rft.au=Schleifer%2C+Theodore&amp;rft.au=Knight%2C+Heather&amp;rft&#95;id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.nytimes.com%2F2026%2F01%2F09%2Ftechnology%2Fgoogle-founders-california-wealth-tax.html&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASergey+Brin" class="Z3988"></span> </span>
